                        cas_cit12R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">12</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Polyanion-type cathode materials for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jin Ting; Li Huangxu; Zhu Kunjie; Wang Peng-Fei; Liu Pei; Jiao Lifang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Society reviews</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">49</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2342-2377</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn"></span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">Room-temperature sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are regarded as promising candidates for smart grids and large-scale energy storage systems (EESs) due to their significant benefits of abundant and low-cost sodium resource.  Among the previously reported cathode materials for SIBs, layered transition-metal oxides and polyanion-type materials are considered to be the most attractive options.  Although many layered transition-metal oxides can provide high capacity due to their small molecular weight, their further application is hindered by low output voltage (mostly lower than 3.5 V), irreversible phase transition as well as storage instability.  Comparatively, polyanion-type materials exhibit higher operating potentials due to the inductive effect of polyanion groups.  Their robust 3D framework significantly decreases the structural variations during sodium ion de/intercalation.  Moreover, the effect of strong X-O (X = S, P, Si, etc.) covalent bonds can effectively inhibit oxygen evolution.  These advantages contribute to the superior cycle stability and high safety of polyanion-type materials.  However, low electronic conductivity and limited capacity still restrict their further application.  This review summarizes the recent progress of polyanion-type materials for SIBs, which include phosphates, fluorophosphates, pyrophosphates, mixed phosphates, sulfates, and silicates.  We also discuss the remaining challenges and corresponding strategies for polyanion-type materials.  We hope this review can provide some insights into the development of polyanionic materials.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref13" class="refNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit13" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.2c12685"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Su, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mo, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ran, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, F.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Na<sup>+</sup>-Activation Engineering in the Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> Cathode with Boosting Kinetics for Fast-Charging Na-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>14</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">47685</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">47695</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acsami.2c12685</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D14%26publication_year%3D2022%26pages%3D47685-47695%26journal%3DACS%2BAppl.%2BMater.%2BInterfaces%26author%3DX.%2BShen%26author%3DY.%2BSu%26author%3DN.%2BYang%26author%3DX.%2BJiang%26author%3DX.%2BLiu%26author%3DJ.%2BMo%26author%3DY.%2BRan%26author%3DF.%2BWu%26title%3DNa%252B-Activation%2BEngineering%2Bin%2Bthe%2BNa3V2%2528PO4%25293%2BCathode%2Bwith%2BBoosting%2BKinetics%2Bfor%2BFast-Charging%2BNa-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsami.2c12685&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsnano.4c18519&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsami.2c12685&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na+-Activation Engineering in the Na3V2(PO4)3 Cathode with Boosting Kinetics for Fast-Charging Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Shen, Xing; Su, Yuefeng; Yang, Ni; Jiang, Xiaoping; Liu, Xingxing; Mo, Junlin; Ran, Yan; Wu, Feng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">14</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">42</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">47685-47695</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na superionic conductor-structured phosphates have attracted wide interest due to their high working voltage and fast Na+ migration facilitated by the robust 3-dimensional open framework.  However, they usually suffer from low-rate capability and inferior cycling stability due to the low intrinsic electronic cond. and limited activated Na+ ions.  Herein, a doping protocol with Na+ in the V3+ site is developed to activate extra electrochem. Na+ ions and expand the migration path of Na+, leading to the improvement of the electronic cond. and diffusion kinetics.  It is also disclosed that the generated stronger Na-O bonds with high ionicity significantly conduce to the enhanced structural stability in the Na+-substituted Na3.05V1.975Na0.025(PO4)3/C cathode.  The obtained composite can deliver an excellent rate capacity of 83.8 mA h g-1 at 20 C and a moderate cycling persistence of 91.3% over 1500 cycles at 10 C with great fast-charging properties.  The reversible structure evolution is confirmed by the ex situ XRD, XPS, and ICP characterization.  This work sheds light on awakening electroactive Na+ ions and designing phosphates with superior electrochem. stability for practical Na-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref14" class="refNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit14" data-doi="10.1038/s41467-023-39384-7"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cui, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, W.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Bridging Multiscale Interfaces for Developing Ionically Conductive High-Voltage Iron Sulfate-Containing Sodium-Based Battery Positive Electrodes</span>. <i>Nat. Commun.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>14</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">3701</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1038/s41467-023-39384-7</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D14%26publication_year%3D2023%26pages%3D3701%26journal%3DNat.%2BCommun.%26author%3DJ.%2BZhang%26author%3DY.%2BYan%26author%3DX.%2BWang%26author%3DY.%2BCui%26author%3DZ.%2BZhang%26author%3DS.%2BWang%26author%3DZ.%2BXie%26author%3DP.%2BYan%26author%3DW.%2BChen%26title%3DBridging%2BMultiscale%2BInterfaces%2Bfor%2BDeveloping%2BIonically%2BConductive%2BHigh-Voltage%2BIron%2BSulfate-Containing%2BSodium-Based%2BBattery%2BPositive%2BElectrodes%26doi%3D10.1038%252Fs41467-023-39384-7&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsnano.4c18519&amp;doiOfLink=10.1038%2Fs41467-023-39384-7&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit14R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">14</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Bridging multiscale interfaces for developing ionically conductive high-voltage iron sulfate-containing sodium-based battery positive electrodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Jiyu; Yan, Yongliang; Wang, Xin; Cui, Yanyan; Zhang, Zhengfeng; Wang, Sen; Xie, Zhengkun; Yan, Pengfei; Chen, Weihua</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">14</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3701</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NCAOBW</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2041-1723</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Portfolio</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Non-aq. sodium-ion batteries (SiBs) are a viable electrochem. energy storage system for grid storage.  However, the practical development of SiBs is hindered mainly by the sluggish kinetics and interfacial instability of pos.-electrode active materials, such as polyanion-type iron-based sulfates, at high voltage.  Here, to circumvent these issues, we proposed the multiscale interface engineering of Na2.26Fe1.87(SO4)3, where bulk heterostructure and exposed crystal plane were tuned to improve the Na-ion storage performance.  Physicochem. characterizations and theor. calcns. suggested that the heterostructure of Na6Fe(SO4)4 phase facilitated ionic kinetics by densifying Na-ion migration channels and lowering energy barriers.  The (11-2) plane of Na2.26Fe1.87(SO4)3 promoted the adsorption of the electrolyte soln. ClO4- anions and fluoroethylene carbonate mols., which formed an inorg.-rich Na-ion conductive interphase at the pos. electrode.  When tested in combination with a presodiated FeS/carbon-based neg. electrode in lab.- scale single-layer pouch cell configuration, the Na2.26Fe1.87(SO4)3-based pos. electrode enables an initial discharge capacity of about 83.9 mAh g-1, an av. cell discharge voltage of 2.35 V and a specific capacity retention of around 97% after 40 cycles at 24 mA g-1 and 25 °C.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref15" class="refNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit15" data-doi="10.1021/acs.nanolett.2c04465"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuan, S.</span></span>;                         cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Solid-Solid Interfacial Charge Storage of Prussian Blue/rGO Mixed-Conductor Cathode for High-Power Na Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Jing; Zhang, Jiliang; Wang, Haihua; Lau, Vincent Wing-hei; Lee, Gi-Hyeok; Zhang, Kai; Park, Mihui; Kang, Yong-Mook</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Energy Letters</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">For the cathode materials potentially available for high power capability, reducing their particle size can improve the bulk ionic cond. due to reduced ion diffusion length, and exploiting new reaction mechanisms must be fundamentally advantageous.  However, other issues such as synthesis difficulty, poor charge-storage stability, and capacity decay can emerge.  To simultaneously address these issues, in this work, we discover a reversible solid-solid interfacial storage in the space-charge region of ultrafine Prussian blue analogs (PBAs)/reduced graphene oxide (rGO), a mixed ion/electron conductor through a so-called "job-sharing" mechanism.  This mechanism shows that electrons and ions can be stored in the different phases around the interface and transport only inside there, which looks thermodynamically distinct from most conventional charge-storage mechanisms in terms of the relationship between charge storage and cell voltage.  The insertion cathodes governed by the job-sharing mechanism thus exhibit outstanding performance with high capacity, fast kinetics, and stable cyclability.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref18" class="refNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit18" data-doi="10.1021/acssuschemeng.0c05466"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zuo, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qiu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lin, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Oriented Formation of a Prussian Blue Nanoflower as a High Performance Cathode for Sodium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ACS Sustainable Chem. However, the shape-controlled prepn. of PB still remains challenging up to now.  Herein, we demonstrate an oriented self-assembly strategy to synthesize PB with three-dimensional (3D) flowerlike structures for the first time, exptl. realizing control of the flower size. In addn., the flower structures can retain their parent structure when undergoing multiple charge-discharge cycles, further confirming the structural stability.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium superionic conductor (NASICON) cathodes are attractive for Na-ion battery applications as they exhibit both high structural stability and high sodium ion mobility.  Herein, a comprehensive study is presented on the structural and electrochem. properties of the NASICON-Na3+yV2-yMny(PO4)3 (0 = y = 1) series.  A phase miscibility gap is obsd. at y = 0.5, defining two solid soln. domains with low and high Mn contents.  Although, members of each of these domains Na3.25V1.75Mn0.25(PO4)3 and Na3.75V1.25Mn0.75(PO4)3 reversibly exchange sodium ions with high structural integrity, the activity of the Mn3+/Mn2+ redox couple is found to be absent and present in the former and latter candidate, resp.  Galvanostatic cycling and rate studies reveal higher capacity and rate capability for the Na3.75V1.25Mn0.75(PO4)3 cathode (100 and 89 mA h g-1 at 1C and 5C rate, resp.) in the Na3+yV2-yMny(PO4)3 series.  Such a remarkable performance is attributed to optimum bottleneck size (~ 5 Å2) and modulated V- and Mn-redox centers as deduced from Rietveld anal. and DFT calcns., resp.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref21"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref21" class="refNumLink">21</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit21" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2023.02.005"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jin, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Recent Progress of Mn-Based NASICON-Type Sodium Ion Cathodes</span>. <i>Energy Storage Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>57</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">69</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">80</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit22R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">22</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Exploring Highly Reversible 1.5-Electron Reactions (V3+/V4+/V5+) in Na3VCr(PO4)3 Cathode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Rui; Xu, Guiliang; Li, Qi; Zheng, Shiyao; Zheng, Guorui; Gong, Zhengliang; Li, Yixiao; Kruskop, Elizaveta; Fu, Riqiang; Chen, Zonghai; Amine, Khalil; Yang, Yong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The development of highly reversible multielectron reaction per redox center in sodium super ionic conductor-structured cathode materials is desired to improve the energy d. of sodium-ion batteries.  Here, the authors studied &gt;1-electron storage of Na in Na3VCr(PO4)3.  Combining advanced characterization techniques such as ex situ 51V solid-state NMR, x-ray absorption near-edge structure, and in situ X-ray diffraction, the authors reveal that V3+/V4+ and V4+/V5+ redox couples in the materials can be accessed, leading to a 1.5-electron reaction.  Also a light change on the local electronic and structural states or phase change could be obsd. after the 1st cycle, resulting in the fast capacity fade at room temp.  Also the irreversibility of the phase changes could be largely suppressed at low temp., thus leading to a much improved electrochem. performance.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref23"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref23" class="refNumLink">23</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit23" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2023.109002"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, W.-H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bai, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Double-Pinning Effect Assisting Na<sub>4</sub>VMn(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> with Superior Structural and Electrochemical Stabilization for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Nano Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2024</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>119</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">109002</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">109011</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na4MnV(PO4)3-rGO as Advanced cathode for aqueous and non-aqueous sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ramesh Kumar, P.; Kheireddine, Aziz; Nisar, Umair; Shakoor, R. A.; Essehli, Rachid; Amin, Ruhul; Belharouak, Ilias</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">429</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">NASICON-type Na4MnV(PO4)3 with reduced graphene oxide (rGO) has been synthesized by the simple sol-gel reaction and characterized by different anal. techniques.  The resulted material has been explored as a cathode material for rechargeable non-aq. and aq. sodium-ion batteries.  In non-aq. electrolytes, the as-synthesized Na4MnV(PO4)3-rGO composite shows stable discharge capacity of 86 mAh g-1 at 0.1 C and 68 mAh g-1 at 0.2 C after 100 cycles in half-cell and full-cell configurations, resp.  In aq. electrolytes, it delivers an initial discharge capacity of 92 mAh g-1 at 1 C rate in half-cells and 97 mAh g-1 at 10 C rate in full-cells having NaTi2(PO4)3-MWCNT as the anode.  Stable cycleability and high rate capabilities of Na4MnV(PO4)3-rGO composite can be attributed to the very strong and sustainable conductive percolation networks for both electrons and Na+ ions.  The obtained results reveal that the aq. electrolyte cell has a huge scope for gird level energy storage applications.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref25" class="refNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit25" data-doi="10.1002/smll.202001524"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lai, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chou, S.-L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Full Activation of Mn<sup>4+</sup>/Mn<sup>3+</sup> Redox in Na<sub>4</sub>MnCr(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> as a High-Voltage and High-Rate Cathode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Small</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>16</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">25</span>), <span class="NLM_elocation-id">e2001524</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/smll.202001524</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D16%26publication_year%3D2020%26journal%3DSmall%26issue%3D25%26author%3DW.%2BZhang%26author%3DH.%2BLi%26author%3DZ.%2BZhang%26author%3DM.%2BXu%26author%3DY.%2BLai%26author%3DS.-L.%2BChou%26title%3DFull%2BActivation%2Bof%2BMn4%252B%252FMn3%252B%2BRedox%2Bin%2BNa4MnCr%2528PO4%25293%2Bas%2Ba%2BHigh-Voltage%2Band%2BHigh-Rate%2BCathode%2BMaterial%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fsmll.202001524&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsnano.4c18519&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fsmll.202001524&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit25R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">25</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Full Activation of Mn4+/Mn3+ Redox in Na4MnCr(PO4)3 as a High-Voltage and High-Rate Cathode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Wei; Li, Huangxu; Zhang, Zhian; Xu, Ming; Lai, Yanqing; Chou, Shu-Lei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">16</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">25</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2001524</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SMALBC</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1613-6810</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Developing high-voltage cathode materials is crit. for sodium-ion batteries to boost energy d.  NASICON (Na super-ionic conductor)-structured NaxMnM(PO4)3 materials (M represents transition metal) have drawn increasing attention due to their features of robust crystal framework, low cost, as well as high voltage based on Mn4+/Mn3+ and Mn3+/Mn2+ redox couples.  However, full activation of Mn4+/Mn3+ redox couple within NASICON framework is still a great challenge.  Herein, a novel NASICON-type Na4MnCr(PO4)3 material with highly reversible Mn4+/Mn3+ redox reaction is discovered.  It proceeds a two-step reaction with voltage platforms centered at 4.15 and 3.52 V vs. Na+/Na, delivering a capacity of 108.4 mA h g-1.  The Na4MnCr(PO4)3 cathode also exhibits long durability over 500 cycles and impressive rate capability up to 10 C.  The galvanostatic intermittent titrn. technique (GITT) test shows fast Na diffusivity which is further verified by d. functional theory calcns.  The high electrochem. activity derives from the 3D robust framework structure, fast kinetics, and pseudocapacitive contribution.  The sodium storage mechanism of the Na4MnCr(PO4)3 cathode is deeply studied by ex situ X-ray diffraction (XRD) and ex situ XPS, revealing that both solid-soln. and two-phase reactions are involved in the Na+ ions extn./insertion process.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref26"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref26" class="refNumLink">26</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit26" data-doi="10.1016/j.ssi.2024.116545"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Deng, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bai, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Rambutan-Like Na<sub>4</sub>MnCr(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>@C/CNTs as a High-Energy-Density Cathode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Solid State Ionics</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2024</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>410</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">116545</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">116552</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Identifying the intrinsic anti-site defect in manganese-rich NASICON-type cathodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yuan; Rong, Xiaohui; Bai, Rui; Xiao, Ruijuan; Xu, Chunliu; Zhang, Chu; Xu, Juping; Yin, Wen; Zhang, Qinghua; Liang, Xinmiao; Lu, Yaxiang; Zhao, Junmei; Chen, Liquan; Hu, Yong-Sheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Energy</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Portfolio</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Manganese-rich NASICON-type materials have triggered widespread attention for developing advanced polyanionic cathodes, primarily driven by their abundant reserves and promising cycling performance with high operating voltages (∼3.8 V for Mn2+/3+/4+, vs. Na+/Na).  However, the charge/discharge profiles exhibit significant voltage hysteresis, which leads to a limited reversible capacity, thereby preventing their application.  Here, we demonstrate that the voltage hysteresis in manganese-rich NASICON-type cathodes (Na3MnTi(PO4)3) is closely related to the intrinsic anti-site defect (IASD), which forms during synthesis and is captured in our characterizations.  Combining electrochem. anal. and spectroscopic techniques, we draw a comprehensive picture of sluggish Na+ diffusion behaviors in the IASD-affected structure during cycling, and rationalize the relationship of voltage hysteresis, phase sepn. and delayed charge compensation.  Furthermore, a Mo-doping strategy is developed to decrease the defect concn., which enhances the initial Coulombic efficiency from 76.2% to 85.9%.  Overall, this work sheds light on the voltage hysteresis in NASICON-type cathodes and provides guidelines for designing high-performance polyanionic electrodes.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref31"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref31" class="refNumLink">31</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit31" data-doi="10.1021/acsenergylett.1c00426"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lin, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xia, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, X.                         cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Improved Performance of Na3TiMn(PO4)3 Using a Non-stoichiometric Synthesis Strategy</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Jiansheng; Lin, Chunfu; Xia, Qingbing; Wang, Chao; Zhao, Xiu Song</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Energy Letters</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na superionic conductor (NASICON)-structured Na3TiMn(PO4)3 (NTMP) is a promising cathode material for sodium-ion batteries.  However, it suffers from a low discharge plateau at about 2.5 V, which leads to not only a substantial capacity decrease in high-voltage discharge plateaus at 4.0 and 3.5 V but also a severe voltage hysteresis.  This work demonstrates that NTMP material synthesized using a non-stoichiometric strategy displays a negligible discharge plateau at 2.5 V and substantially suppressed voltage hysteresis.  The sample also exhibits the highest cycling stability among all polyanionic Mn-based cathode materials, with capacity retention of 91.7% after 2000 cycles. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>35</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">44</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">2304428</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/adma.202304428</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D35%26publication_year%3D2023%26pages%3D2304428%26journal%3DAdv.%2BMater.%26issue%3D44%26author%3DY.%2BZhou%26author%3DG.%2BXu%26author%3DJ.%2BLin%26author%3DY.%2BZhang%26author%3DG.%2BFang%26author%3DJ.%2BZhou%26author%3DX.%2BCao%26author%3DS.%2BLiang%26title%3DReversible%2BMultielectron%2BRedox%2BChemistry%2Bin%2Ba%2BNASICON-Type%2BCathode%2BToward%2BHigh-Energy-Density%2Band%2BLong-Life%2BSodium-Ion%2BFull%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fadma.202304428&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsnano.4c18519&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fadma.202304428&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Reversible Multielectron Redox Chemistry in a NASICON-Type Cathode toward High-Energy-Density and Long-Life Sodium-Ion Full Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhou, Yifan; Xu, Guofu; Lin, Jiande; Zhang, Yangpu; Fang, Guozhao; Zhou, Jiang; Cao, Xinxin; Liang, Shuquan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">35</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">44</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2304428</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADVMEW</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0935-9648</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-superionic-conductor (NASICON)-type cathodes (e.g., Na3V2(PO4)3) have attracted extensive attention due to their open and robust framework, fast Na+ mobility, and superior thermal stability.  To commercialize sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), higher energy d. and lower cost requirements are urgently needed for NASICON-type cathodes.  Herein, Na3.5V1.5Fe0.5(PO4)3 (NVFP) is designed by an Fe-substitution strategy, which not only reduces the exorbitant cost of vanadium, but also realizes high-voltage multielectron reactions.  The NVFP cathode can deliver extraordinary capacity (148.2 mAh g-1), and decent cycling durability up to 84% after 10 000 cycles at 100 C.  In situ X-ray diffraction and ex situ XPS characterizations reveal reversible structural evolution and redox processes (Fe2+/Fe3+, V3+/V4+, and V4+/V5+) during electrochem. reactions.  The low ionic-migration energy barrier and ideal Na+-diffusion kinetics are elucidated by d. functional theory calcns.  Combined with ESR spectroscopy, Fe with unpaired electrons in the 3d orbital is inseparable from the higher-valence redox activation.  More competitively, coupling with a hard carbon (HC) anode, HC//NVFP full cells demonstrate high-rate capability and long-duration cycling lifespan (3000 stable cycles at 50 C), along with material-level energy d. up to 304 Wh kg-1.  The present work can provide new perspectives to accelerate the commercialization of SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref41" class="refNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit41" data-doi="10.1039/D4EE00086B"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tao, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, R.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Confining Hollow ZnSe/NiSe Microspheres in Freestanding Carbon Nanofibers for Flexible Potassium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Energy Environ.                         cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium Ion Storage in Na4MnV(PO4)3@C Free-Standing Electrode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hu, Ping; Zhu, Ting; Cai, Congcong; Mai, Bo; Yang, Chen; Ma, Jianmin; Zhou, Liang; Fan, Hong Jin; Mai, Liqiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">32</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">52</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2208051</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">To enhance the energy d. of batteries and explore intrinsic charge storage mechanism of the active materials, it is important to reduce or eliminate the use of non-active materials in electrodes, such as binder and conductive additives.  Herein, free-standing Na4MnV(PO4)3@C (F-NMVP@C) fiber membrane is fabricated and directly used as a sodium-ion battery (SIB) cathode.  In situ X-ray diffraction reveals that the V3+/V4+ redox reaction occurs through a solid-soln. reaction while a two-phase Mn2+/Mn3+ redox reaction is identified, and both are highly reversible.  Meanwhile, ex situ electrochem. impedance spectroscopy reveals that both the ion diffusion coeff. and charge transfer resistance of F-NMVP@C change reversibly during the Na+ intercalation/de-intercalation.  Battery full cells are assembled based on the free-standing F-NMVP@C cathodes and F-Sb@C anodes, which manifests a high energy d. (293 Wh kg-1) and good cyclability (87.5% after 100 cycles at 1 C).  The high-performance free-standing cathodes and anodes shed light on the development of flexible SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref45"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref45" class="refNumLink">45</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit45" data-doi="10.1002/adsu.202300233"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, S.</span>; <span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Y.</span>; <span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Y.</span>; <span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, H.</span>; <span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, Y.</span>; <span class="NLM_string-name">Du, S.</span>; <span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, W.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Na<sub>4</sub>MnCr(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> with a Dual Conductive Network for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>.  <i>Adv.                 10.1016/j.cej.2021.130680</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D425%26publication_year%3D2021%26pages%3D130680-130687%26journal%3DChem.%2BEng.%2BJ.%26author%3DQ.%2BWang%26author%3DC.%2BLing%26author%3DJ.%2BLi%26author%3DH.%2BGao%26author%3DZ.%2BWang%26author%3DH.%2BJin%26title%3DExperimental%2Band%2BTheoretical%2BInvestigation%2Bof%2BNa4MnAl%2528PO4%25293%2BCathode%2BMaterial%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.cej.2021.130680&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsnano.4c18519&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.cej.2021.130680&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit46R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">46</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Experimental and theoretical investigation of Na4MnAl(PO4)3 cathode material for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Qianchen; Ling, Chen; Li, Jingbo; Gao, Hongcai; Wang, Zongguo; Jin, Haibo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">425</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">130680</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMEJAJ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1385-8947</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Finding appropriate structures of cathode materials is crucial to the development of sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  A novel NASICON-related structure (R-32 space group) of Na4MnAl(PO4)3 is synthesized, which exhibits a high specific capacity (116.8 mAh g-1) with two voltage plateaus of ∼ 3.56 V and ∼ 4.10 V for Mn3+/Mn2+ and Mn4+/Mn3+ redox couples, resp.  The sodium ion storage mechanism and diffusion mechanism are investigated by ex-situ XRD and ex-situ XPS, with the aid of first principle calcns.  Both two-phase and solid soln. reactions take place in the charge/discharge process, and the diffusion path along Na(1) ↔ Na(2) ↔ Na(3) is revealed for the first time in NASICON-structured materials.  In addn., a voltage plateau of ∼ 4.48 V of the Mn5+/Mn4+ redox couple is suggested by the DFT calcns. in Na4MnAl(PO4)3, which may be more easily accessed than that of other compds. such as Na3MnTi(PO4)3 and Na3MnZr(PO4)3 reported in literature, leaving great potential in elevating the voltage and specific capacity for Na4MnAl(PO4)3 cathode.  Because of high theor. specific capacity, high voltage plateaus and low cost, Na4MnAl(PO4)3 is a strong contender in cathode material for SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref47"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref47" class="refNumLink">47</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit47" data-doi="10.1016/j.jelechem.2021.115597"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dai, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">F-Doping Improves the Electrochemical Performance of Na<sub>2</sub>VTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> as the Cathode for Sodium-Ion Battery</span>. <i>J. Electroanal. Chem.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2021</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>900</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">115597</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">115604</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.jelechem.2021.115597</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D900%26publication_year%3D2021%26pages%3D115597-115604%26journal%3DJ.%2BElectroanal.%2BChem.%26author%3DK.%2BSong%26author%3DY.%2BZhu%26author%3DY.%2BJiang%26author%3DX.%2BWang%26author%3DJ.%2BMa%26author%3DC.%2BDai%26author%3DL.%2BZhao%26title%3DF-Doping%2BImproves%2Bthe%2BElectrochemical%2BPerformance%2Bof%2BNa2VTi%2528PO4%25293%2Bas%2Bthe%2BCathode%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BBattery%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.jelechem.2021.115597&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsnano.4c18519&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.jelechem.2021.115597&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit47R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">47</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">F-Doping improves the electrochemical performance of Na2VTi(PO4)3 as the cathode for sodium-ion battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Song, Kexin; Zhu, Yulong; Jiang, Yingying; Wang, Xiuli; Ma, Jifu; Dai, Changsong; Zhao, Li</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Electroanalytical Chemistry</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">900</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">115597</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JECHES</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1873-2569</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Herein, Na super ionic conductor-structured Na2-2xVTi(PO4)3-xFx/C (denoted as NVTP-Fx, x = 0.01, 0.03 and 0.05) is achieved through a simple sol-gel method.  It is the first time that fluorine is introduced in NVTP material, which enhanced the ion/electron transmission of materials, leading to the better rate performance and outstanding cycle life.  Proper fluorine doping demonstrates no significant impact on morphol. of composites.  But the electrochem. performance of the Na2VTi(PO4)3 material has been significantly improved.  The best NVTP-F0.03 sample achieves high discharge specific capacities of 134.3, 82.1, and 75.4 mAh g-1 at 0.1, 5, and 10C (1C = 125 mA g-1), resp.  The capacity retention is as high as 96.5% at 0.5C over 100 cycles, equivalenting to only 0.035% capacity loss per cycle.  At a higher c.d. of 2C, it retains 81.3% capacity after 500 cycles, higher than that of the pristine sample (51.7%).  The elec. anal. results show that the Na+ diffusion kinetics has been greatly improved after fluorine doping, and the carbon coating effectively promotes the charge transfer of electrode.  The results reveal that fluorine doping is a simple and valid strategy to improve the electrochem. performance of NVTP material.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref48"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref48" class="refNumLink">48</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit48" data-doi="10.1039/D1TA05000A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Butenko, D.                         cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">An elaborate insight of lithiation behavior of V2O5 anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yan, Bo; Li, Xifei; Fu, Xinyuan; Zhang, Lulu; Bai, Zhimin; Yang, Xuelin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">78</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">105233</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANCA</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2211-2855</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Vanadium pentoxide (V2O5) has been a promising insert-type cathode material and/or a potential high energy anode material for rechargeable lithium ion batteries (LIBs).  However, the lithiation behavior of V2O5 anode has been a long-standing challenge.  In this study, we design nanoflake-assembled three-dimensional hollow porous V2O5 microspheres via a one-step template-free solvothermal-based method to enhance its structural stability as well as electrochem. activity.  Commendably, this original product evaluated as anode electrodes for LIBs exhibits outstanding cycling stability and rate capability.  It delivers a high reversible capacity of 527 mAh g-1 after 100 cycles at 0.1 A g-1, and a stable capacity of 318 mAh g-1 at 3.0 A g-1 in the potential range of 0.01 V and 3.0 V (vs. Li/Li+).  Furthermore, electrode kinetics and performance evolution was studied by use of electrochem. impedance spectroscopy (EIS).  Following these efforts, a definite and tenable lithiation mechanism of V2O5 anode is presented based on redox behaviors, X-ray powder diffraction (XRD) results, and other convincing proofs, providing valuable revelation for the understanding of conversion reaction and reaction mechanism toward other vanadium oxide anode materials in lithium/sodium ions storage.  Meanwhile, the research perspective and strategy presented herein can be extended to other active materials in LIBs and/or sodium ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref51"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref51" class="refNumLink">51</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit51" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2019.11.004"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lai, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiao, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Highly Efficient Fast and Reversible Multi-Electron Reaction of Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> Cathode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Energy Storage Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>26</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">325</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">333</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>32</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">11</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">1906348</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/adma.201906348</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D32%26publication_year%3D2020%26pages%3D1906348%26journal%3DAdv.%2BMater.%26issue%3D11%26author%3DJ.%2BZhang%26author%3DY.%2BLiu%26author%3DX.%2BZhao%26author%3DL.%2BHe%26author%3DH.%2BLiu%26author%3DY.%2BSong%26author%3DS.%2BSun%26author%3DQ.%2BLi%26author%3DX.%2BXing%26author%3DJ.%2BChen%26title%3DA%2BNovel%2BNASICON-Type%2BNa4MnCr%2528PO4%25293%2BDemonstrating%2Bthe%2BEnergy%2BDensity%2BRecord%2Bof%2BPhosphate%2BCathodes%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fadma.201906348&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsnano.4c18519&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fadma.201906348&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit53R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">53</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A Novel NASICON-Type Na4MnCr(PO4)3 Demonstrating the Energy Density Record of Phosphate Cathodes for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Jian; Liu, Yongchang; Zhao, Xudong; He, Lunhua; Liu, Hui; Song, Yuzhu; Sun, Shengdong; Li, Qiang; Xing, Xianran; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">32</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1906348</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADVMEW</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0935-9648</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries (SIBs) have attracted incremental attention as a promising candidate for grid-scale energy-storage applications.  To meet practical requirements, searching for new cathode materials with high energy d. is of great importance.  Herein, a novel Na superionic conductor (NASICON)-type Na4MnCr(PO4)3 is developed as a high-energy cathode for SIBs.  The Na4MnCr(PO4)3 nanoparticles homogeneously embedded in a C matrix can present an extraordinary reversible capacity of 160.5 mA-h g-1 with 3-electron reaction at ≈3.53 V during the Na+ extn./insertion process, realizing an unprecedentedly high energy d. of 566.5 Wh kg-1 in the phosphate cathodes for SIBs.  It is intriguing to reveal the underlying mechanism of the unique Mn2+/Mn3+, Mn3+/Mn4+, and Cr3+/Cr4+ redox couples via x-ray absorption near-edge structure spectroscopy.  The whole electrochem. reaction undergoes highly reversible single-phase and biphasic transitions with a moderate vol. change of 7.7% through in situ x-ray diffraction and ex situ high-energy synchrotron X-ray diffraction.  Combining d. functional theory (DFT) calcns. with the galvanostatic intermittent titrn. technique, the superior performance is ascribed to the low ionic-migration energy barrier and desirable Na-ion diffusion kinetics.  The present work can offer a new insight into the design of multielectron-reaction cathode materials for SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref54"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref54" class="refNumLink">54</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit54" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2022.107396"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Engineering Hierarchical Structure and Surface of Na<sub>4</sub>MnV(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> for Ultrafast Sodium Storage by a Scalable Ball Milling Approach</span>. <i>Nano Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>99</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">107396</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">107406</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.nanoen.2022.107396</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D99%26publication_year%3D2022%26pages%3D107396-107406%26journal%3DNano%2BEnergy%26author%3DL.%2BZhu%26author%3DM.%2BZhang%26author%3DL.%2BYang%26author%3DK.%2BZhou%26author%3DY.%2BWang%26author%3DD.%2BSun%26author%3DY.%2BTang%26author%3DH.%2BWang%26title%3DEngineering%2BHierarchical%2BStructure%2Band%2BSurface%2Bof%2BNa4MnV%2528PO4%25293%2Bfor%2BUltrafast%2BSodium%2BStorage%2Bby%2Ba%2BScalable%2BBall%2BMilling%2BApproach%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.nanoen.2022.107396&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsnano.4c18519&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.nanoen.2022.107396&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit54R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">54</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Engineering hierarchical structure and surface of Na4MnV(PO4)3 for ultrafast sodium storage by a scalable ball milling approach</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhu, Lin; Zhang, Mengjie; Yang, Lixuan; Zhou, Kexin; Wang, Yan; Sun, Dan; Tang, Yougen; Wang, Haiyan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">99</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">107396</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANCA</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2211-2855</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Polyanion-type Na4MnV(PO4)3 (NMVP) is attracting increasing attention as a cathode material for Na-ion batteries (NIBs) due to its high redox potential and crystal structure stability, while it is still suffering from poor intrinsic cond.  Herein, to address such issue, a unique hierarchical bayberry-like NMVP@NC material, in which the ultra-small primary nanoparticles are embedded in N-doped carbon conductive network, is fabricated by a scalable ball milling approach.  The optimum NMVP@NC electrode exhibits a high reversible capacity of 103.5 mAh g-1 at 0.5 C and maintains a desirable capacity of 82.4 mAh g-1 even at an ultrahigh rate of 100 C.  After 1000 cycles at 5 C, a capacity retention ratio of 94.4% is achieved.  The underlying electrochem. Na storage mechanism verified by the kinetic anal. and operando X-ray diffraction characterization reveals that the superior electrochem. performance should be attributed to the hierarchical structure with a facile ion/electron diffusion pathway and excellent interfacial compatibility.  Moreover, a solid-soln. and biphasic reaction mechanism for Na storage is confirmed in NMVP.  Further demonstration of com. soft carbon//NMVP@NC full cell manifests the good potential of as-prepd. material for practical applications.  Therefore, the NMVP@NC with rational architecture design is a considerable competitive cathode for the commercialization of NIB.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref55"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref55" class="refNumLink">55</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit55" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.202001289"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Polyanion Sodium Vanadium Phosphate for Next Generation of Sodium-Ion Batteries-A Review</span>. <i>Adv. Funct. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>30</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">34</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">2001289</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/adfm.202001289</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D30%26publication_year%3D2020%26pages%3D2001289%26journal%3DAdv.%2BFunct.%2BMater.%26issue%3D34%26author%3DG.%2BChen%26author%3DQ.%2BHuang%26author%3DT.%2BWu%26author%3DL.%2BLu%26title%3DPolyanion%2BSodium%2BVanadium%2BPhosphate%2Bfor%2BNext%2BGeneration%2Bof%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries-A%2BReview%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fadfm.202001289&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsnano.4c18519&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fadfm.202001289&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit55R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">55</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Review on polyanion sodium vanadium phosphate for next generation of sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Gongxuan; Huang, Qing; Wu, Tian; Lu, Li</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">30</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">34</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2001289</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1616-301X</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Polyanion-type sodium (Na) vanadium phosphate in the form of Na3V2(PO4)3 has demonstrated reasonably high capacity, good rate capability, and excellent cyclability.  Two of three Na ions per formula can be deintercalated at a potential 3.4 V vs. Na+/Na with oxidn. of V3+/4+.  In the reversible process, two Na ions intercalate back resulting in a discharge capacity of 117.6 mAh g-1.  Further intercalation is possible but at a low potential of 1.4 V vs. Na+/Na accompanied by vanadium redn. V3+/2+, leading to a capacity of 60 mAh g-1.  Due to its marvelous electrochem. performance, it has attracted a lot of attention since its discovery in the 1990s.  To develop truly useable polyanion-type vanadium phosphate, better understanding of its crystal configuration, sodium ions transportation, and electronic structure is essential.  Therefore, this review only focuses on the inside of crystal configuration and electronic structure of polyanion-type vanadium phosphate, Na3V2(PO4)3, since there are a few good reviews on various processing technologies.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref56"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref56" class="refNumLink">56</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit56" data-doi="10.1103/PhysRevB.59.1758"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kresse, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Joubert, D.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">From Ultrasoft Pseudopotentials to the Projector Augmented-Wave Method</span>. <i>Phys. Rev. B</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">1999</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>59</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1758</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">1775</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit56R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">56</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">From ultrasoft pseudopotentials to the projector augmented-wave method</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kresse, G.; Joubert, D.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Physical Review B: Condensed Matter and Materials Physics</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">1999</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">59</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1758-1775</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">PRBMDO</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0163-1829</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Physical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The formal relationship between ultrasoft (US) Vanderbilt-type pseudopotentials and Blochl's projector augmented wave (PAW) method is derived.  The total energy functional for US pseudopotentials can be obtained by linearization of two terms in a slightly modified PAW total energy functional.  The Hamilton operator, the forces, and the stress tensor are derived for this modified PAW functional.  A simple way to implement the PAW method in existing plane-wave codes supporting US pseudopotentials is pointed out.  In addn., crit. tests are presented to compare the accuracy and efficiency of the PAW and the US pseudopotential method with relaxed-core all-electron methods.  These tests include small mols. (H2, H2O, Li2, N2, F2, BF3, SiF4) and several bulk systems (diamond, Si, V, Li, Ca, CaF2, Fe, Co, Ni).  Particular attention is paid to the bulk properties and magnetic energies of Fe, Co, and Ni.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref57"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref57" class="refNumLink">57</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit57" data-doi="10.1103/PhysRevLett.77.3865"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Perdew, J. P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Burke, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ernzerhof, M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Generalized Gradient Approximation Made Simple</span>. <i>Phys. Rev.                         cas_cit57R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">57</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Generalized gradient approximation made simple</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Perdew, John P.; Burke, Kieron; Ernzerhof, Matthias</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Physical Review Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">1996</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">77</span>

                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">PRLTAO</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0031-9007</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Physical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Generalized gradient approxns. (GGA's) for the exchange-correlation energy improve upon the local spin d. (LSD) description of atoms, mols., and solids.  We present a simple derivation of a simple GGA, in which all parameters (other than those in LSD) are fundamental consts.  Only general features of the detailed construction underlying the Perdew-Wang 1991 (PW91) GGA are invoked.  Improvements over PW91 include an accurate description of the linear response of the uniform electron gas, correct behavior under uniform scaling, and a smoother potential.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref58"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref58" class="refNumLink">58</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit58" data-doi="10.1103/PhysRevB.48.13115"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kresse, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hafner, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Ab Initiomolecular Dynamics for Open-Shell Transition Metals</span>. <i>Phys.                 10.1103/PhysRevB.48.13115</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D48%26publication_year%3D1993%26pages%3D13115-13118%26journal%3DPhys.%2BRev.%2BB%26author%3DG.%2BKresse%26author%3DJ.%2BHafner%26title%3DAb%2BInitiomolecular%2BDynamics%2Bfor%2BOpen-Shell%2BTransition%2BMetals%26doi%3D10.1103%252FPhysRevB.48.13115&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsnano.4c18519&amp;doiOfLink=10.1103%2FPhysRevB.48.13115&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit58R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">58</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ab initio molecular dynamics for open-shell transition metals</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kresse, G.; Hafner, J.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Physical Review B:  Condensed Matter and Materials Physics</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">1993</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">48</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">17</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">13115-18</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">PRBMDO</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0163-1829</span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">The authors show that quantum-mech. mol.-dynamics simulations in a finite-temp. local-d. approxn. based on the calcn. of the electronic ground state and of the Hellmann-Feynman forces after each time step are feasible for liq. noble and transition metals.  This is possible with the use of Vanderbilt-type "ultrasoft" pseudopotentials and efficient conjugate-gradient techniques for the detn. of the electronic ground state.  Results for liq. copper and vanadium are presented.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref59"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref59" class="refNumLink">59</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit59" data-doi="10.1103/PhysRevB.54.11169"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kresse, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Furthmüller, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Efficient Iterative Schemes Forab Initiototal-Energy Calculations Using a Plane-Wave Basis Set</span>. <i>Phys.                 10.1103/PhysRevB.54.11169</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D54%26publication_year%3D1996%26pages%3D11169-11186%26journal%3DPhys.%2BRev.%2BB%26author%3DG.%2BKresse%26author%3DJ.%2BFurthm%25C3%25BCller%26title%3DEfficient%2BIterative%2BSchemes%2BForab%2BInitiototal-Energy%2BCalculations%2BUsing%2Ba%2BPlane-Wave%2BBasis%2BSet%26doi%3D10.1103%252FPhysRevB.54.11169&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsnano.4c18519&amp;doiOfLink=10.1103%2FPhysRevB.54.11169&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit59R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">59</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Efficient iterative schemes for ab initio total-energy calculations using a plane-wave basis set</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kresse, G.; Furthmueller, J.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Physical Review B: Condensed Matter</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">1996</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">54</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">16</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">11169-11186</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">PRBMDO</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0163-1829</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Physical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The authors present an efficient scheme for calcg. the Kohn-Sham ground state of metallic systems using pseudopotentials and a plane-wave basis set.  In the first part the application of Pulay's DIIS method (direct inversion in the iterative subspace) to the iterative diagonalization of large matrixes will be discussed.  This approach is stable, reliable, and minimizes the no. of order Natoms3 operations.  In the second part, we will discuss an efficient mixing scheme also based on Pulay's scheme.  A special "metric" and a special "preconditioning" optimized for a plane-wave basis set will be introduced.  Scaling of the method will be discussed in detail for non-self-consistent and self-consistent calcns.  It will be shown that the no. of iterations required to obtain a specific precision is almost independent of the system size.  Altogether an order Natoms2 scaling is found for systems contg. up to 1000 electrons.  If we take into account that the no. of k points can be decreased linearly with the system size, the overall scaling can approach Natoms.  They have implemented these algorithms within a powerful package called VASP (Vienna ab initio simulation package).  The program and the techniques have been used successfully for a large no. of different systems (liq. and amorphous semiconductors, liq. simple and transition metals, metallic and semiconducting surfaces, phonons in simple metals, transition metals, and semiconductors) and turned out to be very reliable.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li></ol></div><script type="text/javascript"         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  As a promising alternative to the market-leading lithium-ion batteries, low-cost sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are attractive for applications such as large-scale elec. energy storage systems.  The energy d., cycling life, and rate performance of SIBs are fundamentally dependent on dynamic physiochem. reactions, structural change, and morphol. evolution.  Therefore, it is essential to holistically understand SIBs reaction processes, degrdn. mechanisms, and thermal/mech. behaviors in complex working environments.  The recent developments of advanced in situ and operando characterization enable the establishment of the structure- processing- property- performance relationship in SIBs under operating conditions.  This Review summarizes significant recent progress in SIBs exploiting in situ and operando techniques based on X-ray and electron analyses at different time and length scales.  Through the combination of spectroscopy, imaging, and diffraction, local and global changes in SIBs can be elucidated for improving materials design.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The recent proliferation of sustainable and eco-friendly renewable energy engineering is a hot topic of worldwide significance with regard to combating the global environmental crisis.  To curb renewable energy intermittency and integrate renewables into the grid with stable electricity generation, secondary battery-based elec. energy storage (EES) technologies are regarded as the most promising soln., due to their prominent capability to store and harvest green energy in a safe and cost-effective way.  Due to the wide availability and low cost of sodium resources, sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are regarded as a promising alternative for next-generation large-scale EES systems.  This review discusses in detail the key differences between lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) and SIBs for different application requirements and describes the current understanding of SIBs.  By comparing technol. evolutions among LIBs, lead-acid batteries (LABs), and SIBs, the advantages of SIBs are unraveled.  This review also offers highlights on com. achievements that have been realized based on current SIB technol., focusing on an introduction of five major SIB companies, each with SIB chem. and technol., as well as commercialized SIB products.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Energy prodn. and storage technologies have attracted a great deal of attention for day-to-day applications.  In recent decades, advances in lithium-ion battery (LIB) technol. have improved living conditions around the globe.  LIBs are used in most mobile electronic devices as well as in zero-emission electronic vehicles.  However, there are increasing concerns regarding load leveling of renewable energy sources and the smart grid as well as the sustainability of lithium sources due to their limited availability and consequent expected price increase.  Therefore, whether LIBs alone can satisfy the rising demand for small- and/or mid-to-large-format energy storage applications remains unclear.  To mitigate these issues, recent research has focused on alternative energy storage systems.  Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered as the best candidate power sources because sodium is widely available and exhibits similar chem. to that of LIBs; therefore, SIBs are promising next-generation alternatives.  Recently, sodiated layer transition metal oxides, phosphates and org. compds. have been introduced as cathode materials for SIBs.  Simultaneously, recent developments have been facilitated by the use of select carbonaceous materials, transition metal oxides (or sulfides), and intermetallic and org. compds. as anodes for SIBs.  Apart from electrode materials, suitable electrolytes, additives, and binders are equally important for the development of practical SIBs.  Despite developments in electrode materials and other components, there remain several challenges, including cell design and electrode balancing, in the application of sodium ion cells.  In this article, we summarize and discuss current research on materials and propose future directions for SIBs.  This will provide important insights into scientific and practical issues in the development of SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref5" class="rightTabRefNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit5" data-doi="10.1021/acsenergylett.1c02495"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhan, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hou, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Cationic Size Effect Promoting Dissolution of Nitrate Anion in Ester Electrolyte for Lithium-Metal Batteries</span>. <i>ACS Energy Lett.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>7</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">569</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">576</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
